What does it mean by storage mechanisms?

Implement data validation, transformation, and storage mechanisms

============================================================

SYSTEM:


============================================================

ASSISTANT:
Great catch â€” â€œ**storage mechanisms**â€ in this context usually means:  

---

### 1. **Why Storage Matters in a Streaming Pipeline**
- Kafka itself only keeps messages for a configurable time window (e.g., 7 days).  
- If you want to do **analytics, dashboards, or machine learning**, you need a **long-term store**.  
- Thatâ€™s why, after validation & transformation, data is usually persisted in a database, data lake, or file system.  

---

### 2. **Options for Phase 1**
Since this is a course project, you donâ€™t need to spin up a full data warehouse. Instead, you can demonstrate the concept with:  

- **Local CSV / Parquet files**: Consumer writes validated data to disk for later use.  
- **SQLite/Postgres**: Consumer stores data into a small database table.  
- **In-memory store (pandas DataFrame)**: Just to validate pipeline logic before later phases.  

---

### 3. **How It Fits With Your Consumer**
Right now your consumer reads from Kafka and prints/logs the data.  
Adding storage could mean:  
- After **cleaning** a record, write it to `cleaned_data.csv`.  
- Or, insert into a simple SQLite DB:  

```python
import sqlite3

conn = sqlite3.connect("air_quality.db")
cursor = conn.cursor()

# create table once
cursor.execute("""
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS air_quality (
    datetime TEXT,
    co REAL,
    nox REAL,
    no2 REAL,
    benzene REAL,
    temp REAL,
    rh REAL
)
""")

# inside consumer loop
cursor.execute(
    "INSERT INTO air_quality (datetime, co, nox, no2, benzene, temp, rh) VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?)",
    (record['datetime'], record['CO(GT)'], record['NOx(GT)'], record['NO2(GT)'], record['C6H6(GT)'], record['T'], record['RH'])
)
conn.commit()
```

### 4. **What You Need for Deliverables**
For Phase 1, you donâ€™t need a â€œproduction-readyâ€ data lake.  
âœ… A simple CSV or SQLite store will be **enough to satisfy â€œstorage mechanismsâ€**.  
Later phases could expand into analytics/ML on this stored data.

ğŸ‘‰ Do you want me to extend your **consumer.py** so it writes cleaned data into a CSV file (simplest), or set up a tiny SQLite database so it feels more â€œenterpriseâ€?

============================================================

USER:
What does sqlite do? Does that write all the data to a file kinda like a csv?

============================================================

SYSTEM:


============================================================

ASSISTANT:
Good question! âœ…  

Think of **SQLite** as a **database in a file**. Itâ€™s lightweight, serverless, and doesnâ€™t need to be â€œinstalledâ€ like Postgres or MySQL. Hereâ€™s the key difference compared to a CSV:

---

### **CSV**
- Plain text file (comma-separated values).  
- Very easy to read/write.  
- Good for **simple pipelines** or when you just need to save logs.  
- Downsides: no indexing, no querying beyond reading the whole file into memory, limited data integrity.

---

### **SQLite**
- A **database engine** that stores everything inside a single `.db` file.  
- Lets you run **SQL queries** (`SELECT`, `WHERE`, `JOIN`, etc.) directly against the file.  
- Provides indexing, constraints (e.g., no duplicates), and transactions (safe writes even if something crashes).  
- Good for **structured, queryable storage** without needing a full database server.  
- Downsides: not as fast or scalable as Postgres/MySQL, but perfect for small/medium projects.

---

### **In Practice for Our Project**
- If the course project just wants us to **show storage**, a **CSV output is enough**.  
- If we want to demonstrate a more **realistic production-style pipeline**, SQLite is a neat upgrade:  
  - We can query air quality trends later (e.g., average CO per day).  
  - We can easily validate data integrity.  
  - We can use it as a local â€œmini warehouseâ€ before later ML phases.  

---

ğŸ‘‰ Do you want to stick with **CSV (simplest, no new dependencies)** or try **SQLite (a bit more effort, but looks professional and realistic)?**

============================================================

### âœ… `producer.py` (with batching + simulation)
```python
# producer.py
import pandas as pd
import time
import json
import logging
import sys
import random
from kafka import KafkaProducer
from kafka.errors import KafkaError

# --- Logging setup ---
logging.basicConfig(
    level=logging.INFO,
    format="%(asctime)s [%(levelname)s] %(message)s",
    handlers=[
        logging.StreamHandler(sys.stdout),
        logging.FileHandler("phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/logs/producer.log", mode="w")
    ]
)

TOPIC_NAME = "air_quality"
BATCH_SIZE = 50   # send 50 rows at a time
SLEEP_SECS = 1    # simulate delay between batches

# --- Kafka producer with retries ---
def create_producer():
    for attempt in range(5):
        try:
            producer = KafkaProducer(
                bootstrap_servers="localhost:9092",
                value_serializer=lambda v: json.dumps(v).encode("utf-8"),
                retries=3
            )
            logging.info("âœ… Kafka producer created successfully")
            return producer
        except KafkaError as e:
            wait_time = 2 ** attempt + random.random()
            logging.error(f"âŒ Failed to connect to Kafka (attempt {attempt+1}): {e}")
            logging.info(f"Retrying in {wait_time:.2f} seconds...")
            time.sleep(wait_time)
    sys.exit("Producer could not connect to Kafka after multiple attempts.")

producer = create_producer()

# --- Load and preprocess data ---
df = pd.read_csv("AirQualityData/AirQualityUCI.csv", sep=";")
df = df.dropna(axis=1, how="all")

# --- Hybrid cleaning function ---
def clean_row(row):
    record = row.to_dict()
    record = {k: (None if v == -200 else v) for k, v in record.items()}

    if record.get("CO(GT)") is None:
        return None

    if record.get("T") is None:
        record["T"] = 0

    return record

# --- Stream in batches ---
start_time = time.time()
count = 0

batch = []
for _, row in df.iterrows():
    cleaned = clean_row(row)
    if cleaned:
        batch.append(cleaned)

    if len(batch) >= BATCH_SIZE:
        try:
            producer.send(TOPIC_NAME, value=batch)
            count += len(batch)
            logging.info(f"ğŸ“¤ Sent batch of {len(batch)} records. Total sent={count}")
            batch = []
        except KafkaError as e:
            logging.error(f"Error sending batch: {e}")

        time.sleep(SLEEP_SECS)

# send any leftover
if batch:
    producer.send(TOPIC_NAME, value=batch)
    count += len(batch)
    logging.info(f"ğŸ“¤ Sent final batch of {len(batch)} records. Total sent={count}")

elapsed = time.time() - start_time
logging.info(f"âœ… Completed sending {count} records in {elapsed:.2f}s ({count/elapsed:.2f} msg/sec)")
producer.flush()
```

---

### âœ… `consumer.py` (with CSV export)
```python
# consumer.py
from kafka import KafkaConsumer
import json
import logging
import sys
import time
import pandas as pd
import os

# --- Logging setup ---
logging.basicConfig(
    level=logging.INFO,
    format="%(asctime)s [%(levelname)s] %(message)s",
    handlers=[
        logging.StreamHandler(sys.stdout),
        logging.FileHandler("phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/logs/consumer.log", mode="w")
    ]
)

TOPIC_NAME = "air_quality"
OUTPUT_FILE = "phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/cleaned_air_quality.csv"

consumer = KafkaConsumer(
    TOPIC_NAME,
    bootstrap_servers="localhost:9092",
    auto_offset_reset="earliest",
    enable_auto_commit=True,
    group_id="air-quality-consumer",
    value_deserializer=lambda v: json.loads(v.decode("utf-8"))
)

logging.info("âœ… Consumer connected and waiting for messages...")

processed, dropped, unhealthy_no2 = 0, 0, 0
start_time = time.time()

# Create CSV header if file doesnâ€™t exist
if not os.path.exists(OUTPUT_FILE):
    pd.DataFrame().to_csv(OUTPUT_FILE, index=False)

for msg in consumer:
    try:
        batch = msg.value  # batch of rows
        valid_rows = []

        for event in batch:
            if event.get("CO(GT)") is None:
                dropped += 1
                continue

            if event.get("NO2(GT)") and event["NO2(GT)"] > 200:
                event["NO2_status"] = "Unhealthy"
                unhealthy_no2 += 1
            else:
                event["NO2_status"] = "OK"

            valid_rows.append(event)
            processed += 1

        # Append batch to CSV
        if valid_rows:
            df = pd.DataFrame(valid_rows)
            df.to_csv(OUTPUT_FILE, mode="a", index=False, header=not os.path.getsize(OUTPUT_FILE))
            logging.info(f"ğŸ’¾ Wrote {len(valid_rows)} records to {OUTPUT_FILE}")

        if processed % 100 == 0:
            elapsed = time.time() - start_time
            logging.info(
                f"ğŸ“Š Metrics: {processed} processed | {dropped} dropped | {unhealthy_no2} unhealthy NO2 "
                f"| {(processed/elapsed):.2f} msg/sec"
            )

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"âš ï¸ Error processing batch: {e}")
```

---

### ğŸ”‘ Key changes
- **Producer**
  - Sends messages in batches (`BATCH_SIZE` configurable).
  - Adds delay (`SLEEP_SECS`) between sends for realism.
- **Consumer**
  - Processes full batch at once.
  - Appends cleaned/validated rows to `phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/cleaned_air_quality.csv`.
  - Writes header only once.
  - Logs metrics every 100 processed rows.

---

ASSISTANT:
Got it ğŸ‘ â€” thanks for pasting the logs. The issue isnâ€™t that your code is broken â€” itâ€™s that **the producer never actually started sending batches**. Right now your console logs are only showing **consumer group coordination** (Kafka internals), not your `logging.info("ğŸ“¤ Sent batchâ€¦")` messages.

That usually happens when:

1. **The producer never entered the loop**  
   - Maybe the DataFrame was empty (e.g., file path mismatch, separator wrong).  
   - Check `len(df)` after loading in `producer.py` â€” it should be ~9,471 rows.  

2. **The producer isnâ€™t flushing because messages are buffered**  
   - By default, KafkaProducer is asynchronous â€” if you donâ€™t call `.flush()` after sending, nothing gets pushed immediately.  
   - Weâ€™re batching inside Python (`batch = []`), but Kafka also batches internally. If you donâ€™t force a flush, you may see nothing.

3. **The logs arenâ€™t triggered** because no batch ever filled (`len(batch) < BATCH_SIZE`).  
   - If you stopped the script before hitting 50 rows, nothing would send.  
   - Solution: explicitly send partial batches at the end (we did, but letâ€™s double-check placement).  

---

### ğŸ”§ Fix: Add debug + flush earlier
In `producer.py`, right after loading:

```python
logging.info(f"Loaded dataset with {len(df)} rows")
```

Inside the loop:

```python
if len(batch) >= BATCH_SIZE:
    producer.send(TOPIC_NAME, value=batch)
    producer.flush()  # âœ… force push batch
    logging.info(f"ğŸ“¤ Sent batch of {len(batch)} rows")
    batch = []
    time.sleep(SLEEP_SECS)
```

At the very end:

```python
if batch:
    producer.send(TOPIC_NAME, value=batch)
    producer.flush()
    logging.info(f"ğŸ“¤ Sent final batch of {len(batch)} rows")
```

ASSISTANT:
Ahh youâ€™re right ğŸ‘ â€” you *did* load the CSV in your earlier `producer.py`. The issue is smaller:  

Your batches may not be flushing to Kafka, so nothing shows up on the **consumer side**. KafkaProducer is asynchronous by default, so if you only call `send()` without `flush()` inside the loop, the batch may sit in memory.  

---

### ğŸ”§ Fixes
1. **Confirm data loaded**  
   Add a quick log after loading the CSV:  
   ```python
   logging.info(f"Loaded dataset with {len(df)} rows")
   ```
   That should say ~9,471.

2. **Force flush each batch**  
   Inside your batch loop, right after `producer.send(...)`, add:  
   ```python
   producer.flush()
   ```
   This guarantees the batch leaves the buffer and is written immediately.

3. **Log before sending**  
   Add a debug before send to make sure the loop is running:  
   ```python
   logging.info(f"Preparing to send batch of {len(batch)} rows...")
   ```

---

### âœ… Updated `producer.py` (just key fixes)
```python
# --- Stream in batches ---
start_time = time.time()
count = 0

logging.info(f"Loaded dataset with {len(df)} rows")

batch = []
for _, row in df.iterrows():
    cleaned = clean_row(row)
    if cleaned:
        batch.append(cleaned)

    if len(batch) >= BATCH_SIZE:
        try:
            logging.info(f"Preparing to send batch of {len(batch)} rows...")
            producer.send(TOPIC_NAME, value=batch)
            producer.flush()  # âœ… force flush immediately
            count += len(batch)
            logging.info(f"ğŸ“¤ Sent batch of {len(batch)} records. Total sent={count}")
            batch = []
        except KafkaError as e:
            logging.error(f"Error sending batch: {e}")

        time.sleep(SLEEP_SECS)

# send any leftover
if batch:
    producer.send(TOPIC_NAME, value=batch)
    producer.flush()
    count += len(batch)
    logging.info(f"ğŸ“¤ Sent final batch of {len(batch)} records. Total sent={count}")

elapsed = time.time() - start_time
logging.info(f"âœ… Completed sending {count} records in {elapsed:.2f}s ({count/elapsed:.2f} msg/sec)")
```

ASSISTANT:
Exactly â€” and youâ€™ve spotted the key thing ğŸ¯.  

ğŸ‘‰ The **consumer** code you pasted does **not** load the CSV. Thatâ€™s correct behavior:  
- The **consumer** should *only* read messages from Kafka.  
- The **producer** is the one that loads the CSV and streams it into Kafka.  

---

Hereâ€™s the separation of responsibilities:

### âœ… Producer (where CSV is loaded)
In your `producer.py`, you have this block:

```python
# --- Load and preprocess data ---
df = pd.read_csv("AirQualityData/AirQualityUCI.csv", sep=";")
df = df.dropna(axis=1, how="all")
```

That line **does** load the `AirQualityUCI.csv` file from your `AirQualityData/` folder into a pandas DataFrame.  
Then the producer loops over each row (batching, cleaning, sending to Kafka).  

---

### âœ… Consumer (no CSV input, only output)
Your `consumer.py`:
- Connects to Kafka.  
- Waits for messages on the `air_quality` topic.  
- Processes/validates them.  
- Writes them out to a **new CSV**: `phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/cleaned_air_quality.csv`.  

It never sees the original dataset directly. It only sees what the producer sends.  

---

### ğŸ” Why you might not see â€œLoaded datasetâ€¦â€ logs
If youâ€™re not seeing confirmation, itâ€™s because in the **current producer.py youâ€™re running**, we havenâ€™t added a log right after loading the CSV. Itâ€™s working, but silent.  

You can add:  

```python
logging.info(f"Loaded dataset with {len(df)} rows from AirQualityData/AirQualityUCI.csv")
```

right after the `pd.read_csv(...)` line in `producer.py`. That way youâ€™ll see a message confirming the file was loaded.  

---

âœ… So to summarize:  
- Yes, the producer is loading the CSV.  
- The consumer never should â€” it only handles Kafka messages.  
- To double-check, add a `logging.info(...)` after the `read_csv`.

1. Logs when the CSV loads (with row count).

producer.py:

# producer.py
import pandas as pd
import time
import json
import logging
import sys
import random
from kafka import KafkaProducer
from kafka.errors import KafkaError

# --- Logging setup ---
logging.basicConfig(
    level=logging.INFO,
    format="%(asctime)s [%(levelname)s] %(message)s",
    handlers=[
        logging.StreamHandler(sys.stdout),
        logging.FileHandler("phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/logs/producer.log", mode="w")
    ]
)

TOPIC_NAME = "air_quality"
BATCH_SIZE = 50   # send 50 rows at a time
SLEEP_SECS = 1    # simulate delay between batches

# --- Kafka producer with retries ---
def create_producer():
    for attempt in range(5):
        try:
            producer = KafkaProducer(
                bootstrap_servers="localhost:9092",
                value_serializer=lambda v: json.dumps(v).encode("utf-8"),
                retries=3
            )
            logging.info("âœ… Kafka producer created successfully")
            return producer
        except KafkaError as e:
            wait_time = 2 ** attempt + random.random()
            logging.error(f"âŒ Failed to connect to Kafka (attempt {attempt+1}): {e}")
            logging.info(f"Retrying in {wait_time:.2f} seconds...")
            time.sleep(wait_time)
    sys.exit("Producer could not connect to Kafka after multiple attempts.")

producer = create_producer()

# --- Load and preprocess data ---
df = pd.read_csv("AirQualityData/AirQualityUCI.csv", sep=";")
df = df.dropna(axis=1, how="all")

# --- Hybrid cleaning function ---
def clean_row(row):
    record = row.to_dict()
    record = {k: (None if v == -200 else v) for k, v in record.items()}

    if record.get("CO(GT)") is None:
        return None

    if record.get("T") is None:
        record["T"] = 0

    return record

# --- Stream in batches ---
start_time = time.time()
count = 0

batch = []
for _, row in df.iterrows():
    cleaned = clean_row(row)
    if cleaned:
        batch.append(cleaned)

    if len(batch) >= BATCH_SIZE:
        try:
            producer.send(TOPIC_NAME, value=batch)
            count += len(batch)
            logging.info(f"ğŸ“¤ Sent batch of {len(batch)} records. Total sent={count}")
            batch = []
        except KafkaError as e:
            logging.error(f"Error sending batch: {e}")

        time.sleep(SLEEP_SECS)

# send any leftover
if batch:
    producer.send(TOPIC_NAME, value=batch)
    count += len(batch)
    logging.info(f"ğŸ“¤ Sent final batch of {len(batch)} records. Total sent={count}")

elapsed = time.time() - start_time
logging.info(f"âœ… Completed sending {count} records in {elapsed:.2f}s ({count/elapsed:.2f} msg/sec)")
producer.flush()

consumer.py:

# consumer.py
from kafka import KafkaConsumer
import json
import logging
import sys
import time
import pandas as pd
import os

# --- Logging setup ---
logging.basicConfig(
    level=logging.INFO,
    format="%(asctime)s [%(levelname)s] %(message)s",
    handlers=[
        logging.StreamHandler(sys.stdout),
        logging.FileHandler("phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/logs/consumer.log", mode="w")
    ]
)

TOPIC_NAME = "air_quality"
OUTPUT_FILE = "phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/cleaned_air_quality.csv"

consumer = KafkaConsumer(
    TOPIC_NAME,
    bootstrap_servers="localhost:9092",
    auto_offset_reset="earliest",
    enable_auto_commit=True,
    group_id="air-quality-consumer",
    value_deserializer=lambda v: json.loads(v.decode("utf-8"))
)

logging.info("âœ… Consumer connected and waiting for messages...")

processed, dropped, unhealthy_no2 = 0, 0, 0
start_time = time.time()

# Create CSV header if file doesnâ€™t exist
if not os.path.exists(OUTPUT_FILE):
    pd.DataFrame().to_csv(OUTPUT_FILE, index=False)

for msg in consumer:
    try:
        batch = msg.value  # batch of rows
        valid_rows = []

        for event in batch:
            if event.get("CO(GT)") is None:
                dropped += 1
                continue

            if event.get("NO2(GT)") and event["NO2(GT)"] > 200:
                event["NO2_status"] = "Unhealthy"
                unhealthy_no2 += 1
            else:
                event["NO2_status"] = "OK"

            valid_rows.append(event)
            processed += 1

        # Append batch to CSV
        if valid_rows:
            df = pd.DataFrame(valid_rows)
            df.to_csv(OUTPUT_FILE, mode="a", index=False, header=not os.path.getsize(OUTPUT_FILE))
            logging.info(f"ğŸ’¾ Wrote {len(valid_rows)} records to {OUTPUT_FILE}")

        if processed % 100 == 0:
            elapsed = time.time() - start_time
            logging.info(
                f"ğŸ“Š Metrics: {processed} processed | {dropped} dropped | {unhealthy_no2} unhealthy NO2 "
                f"| {(processed/elapsed):.2f} msg/sec"
            )

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"âš ï¸ Error processing batch: {e}")

============================================================

ASSISTANT:
Yes â€” those rows of only semicolons (`;;;;;;;;;;;;`) are junk rows (basically empty lines with separators). They should be dropped completely, both for cleanliness and because theyâ€™ll cause parsing/analysis problems in Phase 2.  

And youâ€™re right: given the dataset description, we can make the cleaning/validation more robust. Right now, your producerâ€™s `clean_row` only looks at `CO(GT)` and `T`. We can strengthen this by enforcing type checks and validating against expected ranges.

---

### ğŸ” Improvements we can add
1. **Drop junk rows**  
   - Remove rows where *all* fields are NaN or just empty semicolons.

2. **Fix European decimals**  
   - Convert commas (`2,6`) â†’ dots (`2.6`) and cast to `float`.

3. **Validate column types** (based on the dataset info):  
   - `Date`: should parse to `datetime`.  
   - `Time`: should parse to `HH.MM.SS`.  
   - `CO(GT)`, `NOx(GT)`, `NO2(GT)`, etc: numeric.  
   - Sensor values (`PT08...`): numeric.  
   - `T`, `RH`, `AH`: numeric.  

4. **Range checks** (basic sanity, based on domain knowledge + dataset notes):  
   - `CO(GT)`: drop if < 0 or > 50 (since typical is 0.5â€“5).  
   - `NOx(GT)`: drop if < 0 or > 5000.  
   - `NO2(GT)`: drop if < 0 or > 1000.  
   - `T`: should be within -50 to 60 Â°C.  
   - `RH`: should be 0â€“100 %.  
   - `AH`: should be non-negative.  

5. **Flag unhealthy NO2** (keep your consumer logic for `"NO2_status"`).  

---

### Example upgrade for `producer.py` cleaning
```python
def clean_row(row):
    record = row.to_dict()

    # Replace -200 with None
    record = {k: (None if v == -200 else v) for k, v in record.items()}

    # --- Drop junk rows ---
    if all(v is None or str(v).strip() == "" for v in record.values()):
        return None

    # --- Type fixes ---
    # Convert decimal commas â†’ floats
    for k, v in record.items():
        if isinstance(v, str) and "," in v:
            try:
                record[k] = float(v.replace(",", "."))
            except ValueError:
                record[k] = None

    # --- Required field ---
    if record.get("CO(GT)") is None:
        return None

    # --- Range checks ---
    if not (0 <= record.get("CO(GT)", 0) <= 50):
        return None
    if record.get("NOx(GT)") is not None and not (0 <= record["NOx(GT)"] <= 5000):
        return None
    if record.get("NO2(GT)") is not None and not (0 <= record["NO2(GT)"] <= 1000):
        return None
    if record.get("T") is not None and not (-50 <= record["T"] <= 60):
        return None
    if record.get("RH") is not None and not (0 <= record["RH"] <= 100):
        return None
    if record.get("AH") is not None and record["AH"] < 0:
        return None

    # Impute missing T with 0
    if record.get("T") is None:
        record["T"] = 0

    return record
```

---

âœ… This way:  
- Junk `;;;;;;;;;` rows get removed.  
- Commas in decimals wonâ€™t break your analysis later.  
- Type + range checks keep garbage out of your stream.  

---

Would you like me to fully **rewrite your producer.py with this upgraded cleaning function** and keep all the batching/streaming logic as-is, so you can run it and regenerate a cleaner CSV for Phase 2?

    TOPIC_NAME,
    bootstrap_servers="localhost:9092",
    auto_offset_reset="earliest",
    enable_auto_commit=True,
    group_id="air-quality-consumer",

        batch = msg.value  # batch of rows
        valid_rows = []

        for event in batch:
            if event.get("CO(GT)") is None:
                dropped += 1
                continue

            if event.get("NO2(GT)") and event["NO2(GT)"] > 200:
                event["NO2_status"] = "Unhealthy"
                unhealthy_no2 += 1
            else:
                event["NO2_status"] = "OK"

            valid_rows.append(event)
            processed += 1

        # Append batch to CSV
        if valid_rows:
            df = pd.DataFrame(valid_rows)
            df.to_csv(OUTPUT_FILE, mode="a", index=False, header=not os.path.getsize(OUTPUT_FILE))

            elapsed = time.time() - start_time
            logging.info(
                f"ğŸ“Š Metrics: {processed} processed | {dropped} dropped | {unhealthy_no2} unhealthy NO2 "
                f"| {(processed/elapsed):.2f} msg/sec"
            )

        logging.error(f"âš ï¸ Error processing batch: {e}")

ASSISTANT:
Perfect ğŸ‘ Letâ€™s upgrade both files. Iâ€™ll leave your logging, batching, and Kafka logic as-is, but enhance the **cleaning/validation** step in the producer. The consumer doesnâ€™t need major changes, except Iâ€™ll add a small safeguard for empty batches.

### âœ… Updated `producer.py`

```python
# producer.py
import pandas as pd
import time
import json
import logging
import sys
import random
from kafka import KafkaProducer
from kafka.errors import KafkaError

# --- Logging setup ---
logging.basicConfig(
    level=logging.INFO,
    format="%(asctime)s [%(levelname)s] %(message)s",
    handlers=[
        logging.StreamHandler(sys.stdout),
        logging.FileHandler("phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/logs/producer.log", mode="w")
    ]
)

TOPIC_NAME = "air_quality"
BATCH_SIZE = 50   # send 50 rows at a time
SLEEP_SECS = 1    # simulate delay between batches

# --- Kafka producer with retries ---
def create_producer():
    for attempt in range(5):
        try:
            producer = KafkaProducer(
                bootstrap_servers="localhost:9092",
                value_serializer=lambda v: json.dumps(v).encode("utf-8"),
                retries=3
            )
            logging.info("âœ… Kafka producer created successfully")
            return producer
        except KafkaError as e:
            wait_time = 2 ** attempt + random.random()
            logging.error(f"âŒ Failed to connect to Kafka (attempt {attempt+1}): {e}")
            logging.info(f"Retrying in {wait_time:.2f} seconds...")
            time.sleep(wait_time)
    sys.exit("Producer could not connect to Kafka after multiple attempts.")

producer = create_producer()

# --- Load and preprocess data ---
df = pd.read_csv("AirQualityData/AirQualityUCI.csv", sep=";")
df = df.dropna(axis=1, how="all")  # drop completely empty columns
logging.info(f"Loaded dataset with {len(df)} rows and {len(df.columns)} columns")

# --- Hybrid cleaning & validation function ---
def clean_row(row):
    record = row.to_dict()

    # Replace -200 with None
    record = {k: (None if v == -200 else v) for k, v in record.items()}

    # Drop junk rows (all empty or NaN)
    if all(v is None or str(v).strip() == "" for v in record.values()):
        return None

    # Fix European decimal commas â†’ floats
    for k, v in record.items():
        if isinstance(v, str) and "," in v:
            try:
                record[k] = float(v.replace(",", "."))
            except ValueError:
                record[k] = None

    # Required field: CO(GT)
    if record.get("CO(GT)") is None:
        return None

    # Range checks (basic domain sanity)
    if not (0 <= record.get("CO(GT)", 0) <= 50):
        return None
    if record.get("NOx(GT)") is not None and not (0 <= record["NOx(GT)"] <= 5000):
        return None
    if record.get("NO2(GT)") is not None and not (0 <= record["NO2(GT)"] <= 1000):
        return None
    if record.get("T") is not None and not (-50 <= record["T"] <= 60):
        return None
    if record.get("RH") is not None and not (0 <= record["RH"] <= 100):
        return None
    if record.get("AH") is not None and record["AH"] < 0:
        return None

    # Impute missing T with 0
    if record.get("T") is None:
        record["T"] = 0

    return record

# --- Stream in batches ---
start_time = time.time()
count = 0
batch = []

for _, row in df.iterrows():
    cleaned = clean_row(row)
    if cleaned:
        batch.append(cleaned)

    if len(batch) >= BATCH_SIZE:
        try:
            producer.send(TOPIC_NAME, value=batch)
            count += len(batch)
            logging.info(f"ğŸ“¤ Sent batch of {len(batch)} records. Total sent={count}")
            batch = []
        except KafkaError as e:
            logging.error(f"Error sending batch: {e}")

        time.sleep(SLEEP_SECS)

# send leftovers
if batch:
    producer.send(TOPIC_NAME, value=batch)
    count += len(batch)
    logging.info(f"ğŸ“¤ Sent final batch of {len(batch)} records. Total sent={count}")

elapsed = time.time() - start_time
logging.info(f"âœ… Completed sending {count} records in {elapsed:.2f}s ({count/elapsed:.2f} msg/sec)")
producer.flush()
```

### âœ… Updated `consumer.py`

```python
# consumer.py
from kafka import KafkaConsumer
import json
import logging
import sys
import time
import pandas as pd
import os

# --- Logging setup ---
logging.basicConfig(
    level=logging.INFO,
    format="%(asctime)s [%(levelname)s] %(message)s",
    handlers=[
        logging.StreamHandler(sys.stdout),
        logging.FileHandler("phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/logs/consumer.log", mode="w")
    ]
)

TOPIC_NAME = "air_quality"
OUTPUT_FILE = "phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/cleaned_air_quality.csv"

consumer = KafkaConsumer(
    TOPIC_NAME,
    bootstrap_servers="localhost:9092",
    auto_offset_reset="earliest",
    enable_auto_commit=True,
    group_id="air-quality-consumer",
    value_deserializer=lambda v: json.loads(v.decode("utf-8"))
)

logging.info("âœ… Consumer connected and waiting for messages...")

processed, dropped, unhealthy_no2 = 0, 0, 0
start_time = time.time()

# Ensure output file exists
if not os.path.exists(OUTPUT_FILE):
    pd.DataFrame().to_csv(OUTPUT_FILE, index=False)

for msg in consumer:
    try:
        batch = msg.value
        if not isinstance(batch, list):
            continue  # safeguard against non-batch messages

        valid_rows = []
        for event in batch:
            if event.get("CO(GT)") is None:
                dropped += 1
                continue

            if event.get("NO2(GT)") and event["NO2(GT)"] > 200:
                event["NO2_status"] = "Unhealthy"
                unhealthy_no2 += 1
            else:
                event["NO2_status"] = "OK"

            valid_rows.append(event)
            processed += 1

        # Write to CSV
        if valid_rows:
            df = pd.DataFrame(valid_rows)
            df.to_csv(OUTPUT_FILE, mode="a", index=False, header=not os.path.getsize(OUTPUT_FILE))
            logging.info(f"ğŸ’¾ Wrote {len(valid_rows)} records to {OUTPUT_FILE}")

        # Periodic metrics
        if processed % 100 == 0:
            elapsed = time.time() - start_time
            logging.info(
                f"ğŸ“Š Metrics: {processed} processed | {dropped} dropped | {unhealthy_no2} unhealthy NO2 "
                f"| {(processed/elapsed):.2f} msg/sec"
            )

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"âš ï¸ Error processing batch: {e}")
```

ASSISTANT:
Ah â€” that error means `record["CO(GT)"]` is still a **string** for some rows (because pandas reads some columns as `object` when there are commas or mixed data).  

We need to explicitly **coerce numeric fields to floats** before applying range checks. Letâ€™s fix the `clean_row` function so that:

1. After replacing commas with dots, we attempt `float()`.  
2. If conversion fails, set the value to `None`.  
3. Do range checks only if the value is numeric (`isinstance(v, (int, float))`).  

---

### ğŸ”§ Fixed `clean_row`

```python
def clean_row(row):
    record = row.to_dict()

    # Replace -200 with None
    record = {k: (None if v == -200 else v) for k, v in record.items()}

    # Drop junk rows (all empty or NaN)
    if all(v is None or str(v).strip() == "" for v in record.values()):
        return None

    # Normalize numeric values (handle commas + coercion)
    for k, v in record.items():
        if isinstance(v, str):
            # try convert European commas
            if "," in v:
                v = v.replace(",", ".")
            try:
                record[k] = float(v)
            except ValueError:
                record[k] = None

    # Required field: CO(GT)
    co_val = record.get("CO(GT)")
    if co_val is None:
        return None

    # Range checks (only if numeric)
    def in_range(val, low, high):
        return isinstance(val, (int, float)) and low <= val <= high

    if not in_range(co_val, 0, 50):
        return None
    if not in_range(record.get("NOx(GT)"), 0, 5000):
        return None
    if not in_range(record.get("NO2(GT)"), 0, 1000):
        return None
    if not in_range(record.get("T"), -50, 60):
        return None
    if not in_range(record.get("RH"), 0, 100):
        return None
    if record.get("AH") is not None and record["AH"] < 0:
        return None

    # Impute missing T with 0
    if record.get("T") is None:
        record["T"] = 0

    return record
```

---

This way:
- All numeric-like values (`"2,6"`, `"1360"`) get converted to `float`.  
- Strings that canâ€™t be parsed become `None`.  
- Range checks wonâ€™t crash because we only compare numbers.

Exactly â€” thatâ€™s expected behavior ğŸ‘  

Hereâ€™s why:  

- **Producer**:  
  - It has a **finite dataset** (your AirQuality CSV).  
  - Once it streams every row â†’ flushes â†’ logs summary â†’ exits.  
  - Thatâ€™s why you see it close automatically.  

- **Consumer**:  
  - By design, Kafka consumers are **long-running services**.  
  - They wait for *new messages* indefinitely (since a topic might receive more data later).  
  - So it doesnâ€™t close on its own â€” it just keeps listening for more events.  
  - You stop it manually with `Ctrl+C`.  

---

In a *real-world system*:  
- Producers (like IoT sensors) never finish â€” they keep sending.  
- Consumers (like analytics dashboards) also never finish â€” they keep listening.  

In your assignment:  
- Since the dataset is fixed, your producer is *finite*.  
- But itâ€™s still fine that the consumer stays open â€” it shows itâ€™s â€œready for more.â€

That usually happens when:
- The CSV was written **without headers** in the producer or consumer.  
- Or, when Pandas inferred the first row of data as column names.

ğŸ‘‰ Fix: ensure we pass `header=True` only once, and explicitly preserve column names from the dataframe.

# consumer.py
from kafka import KafkaConsumer
import json
import logging
import sys
import time
import pandas as pd
import os

# --- Logging setup ---
logging.basicConfig(
    level=logging.INFO,
    format="%(asctime)s [%(levelname)s] %(message)s",
    handlers=[
        logging.StreamHandler(sys.stdout),
        logging.FileHandler("phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/logs/consumer.log", mode="w")
    ]
)

TOPIC_NAME = "air_quality"
OUTPUT_FILE = "phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/cleaned_air_quality.csv"

consumer = KafkaConsumer(
    TOPIC_NAME,
    bootstrap_servers="localhost:9092",
    auto_offset_reset="earliest",
    enable_auto_commit=True,
    group_id="air-quality-consumer",
    value_deserializer=lambda v: json.loads(v.decode("utf-8"))
)

logging.info("âœ… Consumer connected and waiting for messages...")

processed, dropped, unhealthy_no2 = 0, 0, 0
start_time = time.time()

# Ensure output file exists
if not os.path.exists(OUTPUT_FILE):
    pd.DataFrame().to_csv(OUTPUT_FILE, index=False)

for msg in consumer:
    try:
        batch = msg.value
        if not isinstance(batch, list):
            continue  # safeguard against non-batch messages

        valid_rows = []
        for event in batch:
            if event.get("CO(GT)") is None:
                dropped += 1
                continue

            if event.get("NO2(GT)") and event["NO2(GT)"] > 200:
                event["NO2_status"] = "Unhealthy"
                unhealthy_no2 += 1
            else:
                event["NO2_status"] = "OK"

            valid_rows.append(event)
            processed += 1

        # Write to CSV
        if valid_rows:
            df = pd.DataFrame(valid_rows)
            df.to_csv(OUTPUT_FILE, mode="a", index=False, header=not os.path.getsize(OUTPUT_FILE))
            logging.info(f"ğŸ’¾ Wrote {len(valid_rows)} records to {OUTPUT_FILE}")

        # Periodic metrics
        if processed % 100 == 0:
            elapsed = time.time() - start_time
            logging.info(
                f"ğŸ“Š Metrics: {processed} processed | {dropped} dropped | {unhealthy_no2} unhealthy NO2 "
                f"| {(processed/elapsed):.2f} msg/sec"
            )

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"âš ï¸ Error processing batch: {e}")

ASSISTANT:
Perfect â€” letâ€™s patch both scripts so youâ€™ll (1) **keep Date/Time columns**, (2) **preserve headers in the CSV**, and (3) **log dropped rows in the producer summary**.

Hereâ€™s the revised code:

### âœ… `producer.py`

```python
# producer.py
import pandas as pd
import time
import json
import logging
import sys
import random
from kafka import KafkaProducer
from kafka.errors import KafkaError

# --- Logging setup ---
logging.basicConfig(
    level=logging.INFO,
    format="%(asctime)s [%(levelname)s] %(message)s",
    handlers=[
        logging.StreamHandler(sys.stdout),
        logging.FileHandler("phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/logs/producer.log", mode="w")
    ]
)

TOPIC_NAME = "air_quality"
BATCH_SIZE = 50   # send 50 rows at a time
SLEEP_SECS = 1    # simulate delay between batches

# --- Kafka producer with retries ---
def create_producer():
    for attempt in range(5):
        try:
            producer = KafkaProducer(
                bootstrap_servers="localhost:9092",
                value_serializer=lambda v: json.dumps(v).encode("utf-8"),
                retries=3
            )
            logging.info("âœ… Kafka producer created successfully")
            return producer
        except KafkaError as e:
            wait_time = 2 ** attempt + random.random()
            logging.error(f"âŒ Failed to connect to Kafka (attempt {attempt+1}): {e}")
            logging.info(f"Retrying in {wait_time:.2f} seconds...")
            time.sleep(wait_time)
    sys.exit("Producer could not connect to Kafka after multiple attempts.")

producer = create_producer()

# --- Load and preprocess data ---
df = pd.read_csv("AirQualityData/AirQualityUCI.csv", sep=";")
df = df.dropna(axis=1, how="all")  # drop only fully empty cols
logging.info(f"Loaded dataset with {len(df)} rows and {len(df.columns)} columns")

# --- Hybrid cleaning & validation function ---
def clean_row(row):
    record = row.to_dict()

    # Preserve Date + Time as strings
    if "Date" in record and pd.notna(record["Date"]):
        record["Date"] = str(record["Date"]).strip()
    if "Time" in record and pd.notna(record["Time"]):
        record["Time"] = str(record["Time"]).strip()

    # Replace -200 with None
    record = {k: (None if v == -200 else v) for k, v in record.items()}

    # Drop junk rows (all empty or NaN)
    if all(v is None or str(v).strip() == "" for v in record.values()):
        return None

    # Normalize numeric values (ignore Date/Time)
    for k, v in record.items():
        if k in ["Date", "Time"]:
            continue
        if isinstance(v, str):
            if "," in v:
                v = v.replace(",", ".")
            try:
                record[k] = float(v)
            except ValueError:
                record[k] = None

    # Required field: CO(GT)
    co_val = record.get("CO(GT)")
    if co_val is None:
        return None

    # Range checks
    def in_range(val, low, high):
        return isinstance(val, (int, float)) and low <= val <= high

    if not in_range(co_val, 0, 50):
        return None
    if not in_range(record.get("NOx(GT)"), 0, 5000):
        return None
    if not in_range(record.get("NO2(GT)"), 0, 1000):
        return None
    if not in_range(record.get("T"), -50, 60):
        return None
    if not in_range(record.get("RH"), 0, 100):
        return None
    if record.get("AH") is not None and record["AH"] < 0:
        return None

    # Impute missing T with 0
    if record.get("T") is None:
        record["T"] = 0

    return record

# --- Stream in batches ---
start_time = time.time()
count, dropped = 0, 0
batch = []

for _, row in df.iterrows():
    cleaned = clean_row(row)
    if cleaned:
        batch.append(cleaned)
    else:
        dropped += 1

    if len(batch) >= BATCH_SIZE:
        try:
            producer.send(TOPIC_NAME, value=batch)
            count += len(batch)
            logging.info(f"ğŸ“¤ Sent batch of {len(batch)} records. Total sent={count}")
            batch = []
        except KafkaError as e:
            logging.error(f"Error sending batch: {e}")

        time.sleep(SLEEP_SECS)

# send leftovers
if batch:
    producer.send(TOPIC_NAME, value=batch)
    count += len(batch)
    logging.info(f"ğŸ“¤ Sent final batch of {len(batch)} records. Total sent={count}")

elapsed = time.time() - start_time
logging.info(
    f"âœ… Completed sending {count} records in {elapsed:.2f}s "
    f"({count/elapsed:.2f} msg/sec). Dropped {dropped} invalid rows."
)
producer.flush()
```

---

### âœ… `consumer.py` (small tweak for CSV headers)

```python
# consumer.py
from kafka import KafkaConsumer
import json
import logging
import sys
import time
import pandas as pd
import os

# --- Logging setup ---
logging.basicConfig(
    level=logging.INFO,
    format="%(asctime)s [%(levelname)s] %(message)s",
    handlers=[
        logging.StreamHandler(sys.stdout),
        logging.FileHandler("phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/logs/consumer.log", mode="w")
    ]
)

TOPIC_NAME = "air_quality"
OUTPUT_FILE = "phase_1_streaming_infrastructure/cleaned_air_quality.csv"

consumer = KafkaConsumer(
    TOPIC_NAME,
    bootstrap_servers="localhost:9092",
    auto_offset_reset="earliest",
    enable_auto_commit=True,
    group_id="air-quality-consumer",
    value_deserializer=lambda v: json.loads(v.decode("utf-8"))
)

logging.info("âœ… Consumer connected and waiting for messages...")

processed, dropped, unhealthy_no2 = 0, 0, 0
start_time = time.time()

# Reset output file
if os.path.exists(OUTPUT_FILE):
    os.remove(OUTPUT_FILE)

for msg in consumer:
    try:
        batch = msg.value
        if not isinstance(batch, list):
            continue

        valid_rows = []
        for event in batch:
            if event.get("CO(GT)") is None:
                dropped += 1
                continue

            if event.get("NO2(GT)") and event["NO2(GT)"] > 200:
                event["NO2_status"] = "Unhealthy"
                unhealthy_no2 += 1
            else:
                event["NO2_status"] = "OK"

            valid_rows.append(event)
            processed += 1

        # Write to CSV with headers preserved
        if valid_rows:
            df = pd.DataFrame(valid_rows)
            write_header = not os.path.exists(OUTPUT_FILE)
            df.to_csv(OUTPUT_FILE, mode="a", index=False, header=write_header)
            logging.info(f"ğŸ’¾ Wrote {len(valid_rows)} records to {OUTPUT_FILE}")

        if processed % 100 == 0:
            elapsed = time.time() - start_time
            logging.info(
                f"ğŸ“Š Metrics: {processed} processed | {dropped} dropped | {unhealthy_no2} unhealthy NO2 "
                f"| {(processed/elapsed):.2f} msg/sec"
            )

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"âš ï¸ Error processing batch: {e}")
```

3. **Consumer**: resets the output file each run and ensures headers are written once.

ASSISTANT:
You spotted it perfectly ğŸ‘Œ â€” the difference comes from **where the dropping happens**:  

- **Producer side**  
  - Your `clean_row()` does validation (missing values, ranges, etc).  
  - If a row fails â†’ it is **never sent to Kafka**.  
  - Thatâ€™s why the producer logs show **2530 dropped rows**.  

- **Consumer side**  
  - The consumer only sees **what Kafka received**.  
  - Since the producer already filtered out bad rows, the consumer only ever receives valid ones.  
  - Thatâ€™s why your consumer logs show **0 dropped rows** â€” because *nothing invalid reached it*.  

So:  
- âœ… **Producer "Dropped"** = rows rejected before publishing to Kafka.  
- âœ… **Consumer "Dropped"** = rows rejected between Kafka â†’ CSV (but there werenâ€™t any, because producer already handled them).  

---

ğŸ‘‰ In practice:  
- Itâ€™s **normal** that consumer dropped count is zero.  
- You now have **two levels of validation**:  
  1. Producer â†’ ensures only valid rows enter Kafka.  
  2. Consumer â†’ sanity-checks again before writing to storage.  

Thatâ€™s actually good design (defense in depth).  

---

If you want **clearer reporting**, we can:  
- Rename producer log â†’ `Dropped (before send)`  
- Rename consumer log â†’ `Dropped (after receive)`  

So itâ€™s obvious *when* the row was discarded.  

Would you like me to adjust the log messages in both scripts to make that distinction explicit?

## ğŸ“„ setup_and_architecture.md

### Kafka Setup and Configuration
- **Version**: Apache Kafka **3.9.1** (last release with ZooKeeper).  
- **ZooKeeper**: Required for broker coordination. Launched via `bin/zookeeper-server-start.sh config/zookeeper.properties`.  
- **Broker**: Started with `bin/kafka-server-start.sh config/server.properties`.  
- **Topic**: Created `air_quality` with 1 partition and replication factor 1 (sufficient for local development).  
  ```bash
  bin/kafka-topics.sh --create \
    --topic air_quality \
    --bootstrap-server localhost:9092 \
    --partitions 1 \
    --replication-factor 1
  ```

### Architecture Decisions
- **Local Deployment**: Chosen for simplicity and grading â€” no containerization or cluster needed.  
- **ZooKeeper**: Even though ZooKeeper is being phased out, this assignment requires learning fundamentals, so 3.9.1 ensures compatibility.  
- **Single Partition**: Our dataset is relatively small and the goal is correctness, not horizontal scaling. A single partition avoids offset management complexity.  
- **File-Based Logs**: Both producer and consumer log to `logs/` for transparency and monitoring.

### Error Handling and Resilience
- **Producer**: Retry logic with exponential backoff (up to 5 attempts).  
- **Consumer**: Graceful error logging per batch, no crash on malformed data.  
- **Monitoring**: Metrics are logged every 100 rows for throughput, drops, and unhealthy NOâ‚‚ counts.

---

## ğŸ“„ preprocessing_strategy.md

### Dataset Overview
- **Source**: UCI Air Quality Dataset (9,358 hourly sensor observations).  
- **Challenges**: Missing values encoded as `-200`, occasional junk rows (`;;;;;;;;;;;;;;;`).  
- **Goal**: Deliver cleaned, validated data suitable for real-time ingestion.

### Hybrid Preprocessing Approach
We adopted a **hybrid strategy**, splitting responsibilities between producer and consumer.

#### Producer-Side Cleaning (before Kafka)
- **Why**: Prevents bad data from polluting the stream.  
- **Steps**:
  - Convert `-200` â†’ `None`.  
  - Drop rows with all missing values or invalid types.  
  - Range validation:  
    - CO(GT): 0â€“50 mg/mÂ³  
    - NOx(GT): 0â€“5000 ppb  
    - NO2(GT): 0â€“1000 Âµg/mÂ³  
    - T: -50â€“60 Â°C  
    - RH: 0â€“100 %  
    - AH: â‰¥0  
  - Impute missing temperature (`T`) with 0.  
- **Result**: 6,941 valid rows sent (â‰ˆ2,530 dropped before send).

#### Consumer-Side Validation (after Kafka)
- **Why**: Defense-in-depth + operational checks.  
- **Steps**:
  - Re-validate CO(GT) presence.  
  - Enrich rows with `NO2_status`:
    - `Unhealthy` if NOâ‚‚ > 200 Âµg/mÂ³.  
    - `OK` otherwise.  
  - Append valid batches to `cleaned_air_quality.csv`.  
- **Monitoring**: Logs batch size, throughput, dropped rows (after receiving), and unhealthy NOâ‚‚ counts.

### Quality Metrics
- **Producer**: Reports total rows scanned, valid vs dropped counts.  
- **Consumer**: Reports rows processed, unhealthy percentage, throughput.  
- **Final Dataset**: Cleaned CSV with headers, preserved `Date` + `Time`.

## ğŸ“¤ Ways to Save/Export ChatGPT Conversations

### 1. **Manual Export (built-in)**
- In ChatGPT, click your profile â†’ **Settings â†’ Data Controls â†’ Export Data**.  
- This sends you an email with a `.zip` containing **all your conversations** (JSON + HTML).  
- Downside: itâ€™s everything at once, not just a single chat.

---

### 2. **Copy-Paste + Appendix Workflow**
- For each assignment, copy the **prompt + response** you want to cite into a text/Markdown file.  
- Keep a folder in your project repo called `appendix_ai/` where you save these transcripts.  
- Then link them in your final report appendix.  
  Example:  
  ```
  Appendix A â€“ ChatGPT Usage
  See appendix_ai/setup_doc_chat.txt for full transcript.
  ```

### 3. **Browser Extensions**
- Extensions like **ChatGPT Exporter** or **ChatGPT to Markdown** let you download a single chat directly in `.md` or `.txt`.  
- Useful if you donâ€™t want the full data dump.

---

### 4. **Screenshots (last resort)**
- Some students just take screenshots of the relevant parts and embed them in their Appendix.  
- Not ideal for long conversations but still compliant if the course requires full transparency.
